Second Proof: Exception in Quran 51:36
Taftazani gives the second proof from Quran 51:36 with objection and answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quranic exception in verse 51:36 serves as a proof that iman and Islam are identical in meaning.

Core Idea
Exception in the Quran proves that believers and Muslims are the same group.

Taftazani presents a second argument based on linguistic analysis of a Quranic verse. The verse excepts believers from Muslims, implying that the two terms refer to the same group. An objection is raised about the nature of exception, and the answer clarifies that the required unity is non-separateness, not mere inclusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof from exception
Read how Taftazani constructs the proof: if iman and Islam were different, exception from one to the other would be invalid. The Quranic exception shows they are one.
Note the logical structure: if P then Q, not Q, therefore not P.
2
Examine the objection
An objector argues that exception only requires inclusion, not identity of concept. This would undermine the proof.
The objector uses a narrow understanding of exception.
3
Understand the answer
Taftazani replies that the required unity is non-separateness (la infikak), meaning they cannot be separate categories. The verse's structure shows mutual inclusion.
This preserves the proof while acknowledging the general rules of exception.
4
Consider the additional nuance
Taftazani adds a note about directionality: exception can work from a more general to a less general, but not vice versa. The verse's wording shows that believers are a subset of Muslims, but the exception proves they are the same group.
This strengthens the argument against the objection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وثانيهما - أنه لو كان غيره، لم يصح استثناء أحدهما من الآخر. واللازم باطل، لقوله تعالى : ( فأخرجنا من كان فيها من المؤمنين فما وجدنا فيها غير بيت من المسلمين ) أي فلم نجد ممن كان فيها من المؤمنين إلا أهل بيت من المسلمين. واعترض بأنه يكفي لصحة الاستثناء الإحاطة والشمول بحيث يدخل المستثنى تحت المستثنى منه . ولا يتوقف على اتحاد المفهوم، وقد عرفت أن المراد بالاتحاد عدم التغاير بمعنى الانفكاك، نعم لو قيل: إنه لا يتوقف على المساواة أيضاً، بل يصح مع كون المؤمن أعم كقولك: أخرجت العلماء فلم أترك إلا بعض النحاة، لكان شيئاً لا بالعكس على ما سبق إلى بعض الأوهام، ذهاباً إلى صحة قولنا : أخرجت العلماء فلم أترك إلا بعض الناس.
And the second: that if it were other than it, it would not be valid to except one from the other. The consequent is false, due to His saying, exalted is He: 'So We brought out whoever was in it of the believers, and We did not find in it other than a house of Muslims' (51:36). That is, we did not find among those who were in it of the believers except the people of a house of Muslims. And it was objected that for the validity of exception, sufficiency is encompassment and inclusion such that the excepted enters under the excepted-from. And it does not depend on unity of concept, and you have known that by unity is meant non-differentiation in the sense of separateness. Yes, if it were said that it does not depend on equality either, but it is valid while the believer is more general, as when you say: I brought out the scholars and I did not leave except some of the grammarians, it would be something, not the opposite, as has occurred to some illusions, going to the validity of our saying: I brought out the scholars and I did not leave except some people.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage gives the second proof based on the Quranic verse 51:36, where 'believers' are excepted from 'Muslims', implying they refer to the same group. The objection argues that exception only requires the excepted to be included in the excepted-from, not identity of meaning. The answer clarifies that the required unity is non-separateness (la infikak), meaning they cannot be separate categories. The discussion then adds that even if 'believer' were more general than 'Muslim', exception would work in one direction but not the reverse, and the verse's structure shows mutual inclusion, not mere generality.

Key Terms
الاستثناء
الإحاطة
الشمول
اتحاد المفهوم
الانفكاك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Exception always implies that the excepted and the excepted-from are identical in meaning.
Correction: Exception only requires inclusion; identity is a stronger condition that must be inferred from context. In this verse, the mutual inclusion indicates non-separateness, not mere inclusion.

Checkpoint
Why does the exception in Quran 51:36 prove that iman and Islam are identical?
A) Because exception always requires identity of meaning.
B) Because the believers are excepted from Muslims, showing they are the same group.
C) Because the verse says 'believers' and 'Muslims' are synonyms.
D) Because exception is only valid when the terms are identical.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic exception in verse 51:36 supports the identity of iman and Islam because the excepted group (believers) is exactly the same as the excepted-from group (Muslims), implying non-separateness.

Third Proof: Quranic Interchangeability of Iman and Islam
Taftazani cites Quranic verses as evidence that iman and Islam are used interchangeably.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran uses the terms iman and Islam interchangeably, supporting their identity as one reality.

Core Idea
The Quran itself treats iman and Islam as one reality.

Taftazani now offers a third proof: the Quran itself uses 'iman' and 'Islam' in each other's place. Several verses show that those who believe are called Muslims, and those who submit are said to have been guided to faith. This lesson examines those verses and their implication for the identity of the two terms.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get the flow of Taftazani's argument and the Quranic verses he cites.
Notice the pattern: each verse equates or interchanges the two terms.
2
Analyze each verse
Work through each of the four Quranic verses (49:17, 30:53, 3:102, 3:84) and see how they pair iman and Islam. Ask: how does the verse show interchangeability?
In 49:17, 'aslamu' (they became Muslims) is followed by 'hadaakum lil'iman' (guided you to faith).
3
Reflect on the overall argument
Consider why this interchangeability is a strong proof for the identity of iman and Islam. What would it mean if they were different?
This step connects the verses to the broader theological claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد يستدل بسوق أحد الاسمين مساق الآخر، كقوله تعالى: (يمنون عليك أن أسلموا قل لا تمنوا علي إسلامكم بل الله يمن عليكم أن هداكم للإيمان إن كنتم صادقين) و (إن تسمع إلا من يؤمن بآياتنا فهم مسلمون) (يا أيها الذين آمنوا اتقوا الله حق تقاته ولا تموتن إلا وأنتم مسلمون) (قولوا آمنا بالله وما أنزل إلينا) إلى قوله: (ونحن له مسلمون). إلى غير ذلك من الآيات.
And they may adduce by employing one of the two terms in the place of the other, such as His saying, exalted is He: 'They consider it a favor to you that they have become Muslims. Say: Do not consider your Islam a favor to me; rather, Allah has conferred a favor upon you that He has guided you to iman, if you should be truthful' (49:17). And 'And you cannot make hear except those who believe in Our verses, so they are Muslims' (30:53). 'O you who have believed, fear Allah as He should be feared and do not die except as Muslims' (3:102). 'Say, we have believed in Allah and what has been revealed to us...' until His saying: 'and we are Muslims to Him' (3:84). And other verses like these.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage presents a third proof that iman and Islam are identical: the Quran uses the two terms interchangeably. The examples show that 'Islam' is equated with 'iman'. In 49:17, those who 'aslamu' are said to be guided to 'iman'. In 30:53, those who believe are called 'muslimun'. Believers are commanded to die as Muslims (3:102), and they profess both 'amanna' and 'nahnu muslimun' (3:84). This interchangeability supports their identity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Different words always indicate different meanings.
Correction: The Quran itself uses 'iman' and 'Islam' interchangeably, showing they refer to the same essential reality in many contexts.

Key Takeaway

Iman Increases and Decreases: The Apparent Meaning and Majority Opposition
Author states apparent Quranic/Sunnah meaning and majority's opposition with reason.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the initial position that the apparent meaning of Quran and Sunnah supports increase and decrease of iman, and the basis for the majority's denial.

Core Idea
The majority denied increase and decrease because they defined iman as a fixed, indivisible assent.

The third investigation begins by acknowledging the apparent scriptural evidence for iman's increase and decrease. However, the majority of scholars opposed this understanding. Their reasoning is rooted in a specific definition of iman: it is not a matter of degrees but a definitive assent (tasdiq) that has reached a certain threshold. This lesson unpacks this foundational disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and its literal translation. Note that the passage is cut off, but the main idea is clear: the apparent meaning of revelation suggests increase/decrease, but the majority denied it based on the definition of iman.
The passage may be incomplete, but the core point is present.
2
Identify the two sides
Identify the two positions mentioned: the apparent meaning of Quran/Sunnah (implying increase and decrease) and the majority who opposed it.
3
Understand the majority's reason
The text says 'because it is the name for tasdiq that has reached the limit'. Consider what 'limit' (حد) means for the definition of iman. This suggests that iman is a single, complete act of assent, not partial.
The full argument is continued beyond this page.
4
Reflect on the implication
Ask: Why would defining iman as a fixed limit prevent increase and decrease? How does this definition differ from everyday understanding?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : المبحث الثالث - ظاهر الكتاب والسنة (إن الإيمان يزيد وينقص ومنعه الجمهور لما أنه اسم للتصديق البالغ حد...
He said: The third investigation - the apparent meaning of the Book and the Sunnah (that iman increases and decreases, and the majority prevented it because it is the name for tasdiq that has reached the limit...)
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage opens the third investigation of the topic. The author states that the apparent (ظاهر) meaning of the Quran and Sunnah indicates that iman can increase and decrease. However, the majority of scholars (الجمهور) opposed this view. Their reason, as given here, is that iman is the name for tasdiq (assent) that has reached a certain limit (البالغ حد...). The sentence is incomplete, but it suggests that the majority consider iman to be a single, indivisible act of inner assent that does not admit of degrees. The full argument is not present in this window.

Key Terms

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The majority deny any increase in iman, even in actions or certainty.
Correction: The majority deny increase and decrease in the essence of iman (tasdiq) itself, but many affirm variation in its strength or associated actions.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The majority denied iman's increase and decrease because they defined iman as a fixed, indivisible assent (tasdiq) at a limit.

?

Juwayni's View on the Impossibility of Superiority in Tasdiq
Juwayni's argument and the first objection-response cycle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Juwayni's argument that tasdiq does not admit quantitative variation and how the Salafi view reconciles increase and decrease with the distinction between essence and perfection of faith.

Core Idea
Tasdiq does not vary, but its perfection can.

This lesson examines Juwayni's foundational claim that if faith is identified with tasdiq (assent), then no tasdiq can be superior to another. You will also encounter an objection and response that clarify the difference between the essence of faith and its perfection, a key distinction for the Salafi position. Imam al-Razi's reconciliation of seemingly conflicting verses is also introduced.

Guided Path
1
Read Juwayni's statement
Understand the two scenarios Juwayni presents: if faith is tasdiq, and if faith is obedience. Notice his preference.
2
Examine the objection
Consider the objection that if faith is works, it is even less likely to vary. Identify the two reasons given.
The objection argues from 'no rank above the whole' and 'no one can complete faith'.
3
Analyze the response
See how the response distinguishes Mu'tazili vs Salafi views, and introduces the concept of variation in perfection, not essence.
4
Learn al-Razi's reconciliation
Note how Imam al-Razi reconciles conflicting verses: those indicating non-variation refer to essence, those indicating variation refer to perfect faith.
This is a key harmonizing principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال إمام الحرمين : إذا حملنا الإيمان على التصديق ، فلا يفضل تصديق تصديقاً، كما لا يفضل علم علماً . ومن حمله على الطاعة سراً وعلناً ـ وقد مال إليه القلانسي (١) ـ فلا يبعد إطلاق القول بأنه يزيد بالطاعة، وينقص بالمعصية، ونحن لا نؤثر هذا لا يقال: الإيمان على تقدير كونه اسماً للأعمال أولى بأن لا يحتمل الزيادة والنقصان .
أما أولاً فلأنه لا مرتبة فوق الكل ليكون زيادة، ولا إيمان دونه ليكون نقصاناً. وأما ثانياً، فلأن أحداً لا يستكمل الإيمان حينئذ، والزيادة على ما لم يكمل بعد محال . لأنا نقول هذا إنما يرد على من يقول بانتفاء الإيمان بانتفاء شيء من الأعمال أو التروك، كما هو مذهب المعتزلة، لا على من يقول ببقائه ما بقي التصديق، كما هو مذهب السلف، إلا ان الزيادة والنقصان على هذا تكون في كمال الإيمان لا في أصله . ولهذا قال الإمام الرازي وجه التوفيق أن ما يدل على أن الإيمان لا يتفاوت مصروف الى أصله وما يدل على أنه يتفاوت مصروف إلى الكامل منه ولقائل أن يقول : لا نسلم أن التصديق لا يتفاوت، بل يتفاوت قوة وضعفاً، كما في التصديق بطلوع الشمس، والتصديق بحدوث العالم، لأنه إما نفس الاعتقاد القابل للتفاوت أو مبني عليه وقلة وكثرة ، كما في التصديق الإجمالي والتفصيلي الملاحظ لبعض التفاصيل وأكثر وأكثر ، فإن ذلك من الإيمان لكونه تصديقاً بما جاء به النبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) إجمالاً فيما علم إجمالاً ، وتفصيلاً فيما علم تفصيلاً، لا يقال : الواجب تصديق يبلغ حد اليقين، وهو لا يتفاوت لأن التفاوت لا يتصور إلا باحتمال النقيض، لأنا نقول : اليقين من باب العلم والمعرفة، وقد سبق أنه غير التصديق، ولو سلم أنه التصديق، وأن المراد به ما يبلغ حد الإذعان والقبول، ويصدق عليه المعنى المسمى «بكرويدن» ليكون تصديقاً قطعياً، فلا نسلم أنه لا يقبل التفاوت بل لليقين مراتب من أجلى البديهيات إلى أخفى النظريات، وكون
Imam al-Haramayn said: If we carry faith (iman) upon tasdiq (assent), then no tasdiq is superior to another tasdiq, just as no knowledge (ilm) is superior to knowledge. And whoever carries it upon obedience (ta'a) secretly and openly—and al-Qalanisi inclined to that—then it is not unlikely to say that it increases with obedience and decreases with disobedience, but we do not prefer this. It should not be said: Faith, on the assumption that it is a name for works, is more deserving not to admit increase and decrease. First, because there is no rank above the whole to be an increase, nor any faith below it to be a decrease. Second, because no one then would complete faith, and increase upon what is not yet complete is impossible. For we say: This only refutes those who say that faith is negated by the negation of any actions or omissions, as is the doctrine of the Mu'tazilis, not those who say that it remains as long as tasdiq remains, as is the doctrine of the Salaf. Except that increase and decrease, on this, are in the perfection of faith, not in its essence. For this reason, Imam al-Razi said: The way of reconciliation is that what indicates that faith does not vary is directed to its essence, and what indicates that it varies is directed to the perfect form of it. And someone may say: We do not concede that tasdiq does not vary; rather it varies in strength and weakness, as in the tasdiq of the rising of the sun and the tasdiq of the origination of the world, because it is either the belief itself which admits variation or is built upon it, and in fewness and multitude, as in general and detailed tasdiq that observes some details and more and more. For that is part of faith because it is a tasdiq of what the Prophet (peace be upon him) brought, generally in what is known generally, and in detail in what is known in detail. It should not be said: The obligatory tasdiq reaches the level of certainty (yaqin), and it does not vary because variation is only conceivable by the possibility of the opposite. For we say: Certainty is of the category of knowledge and ma'rifa (cognition), and it has preceded that it is other than tasdiq. And even if it is conceded that it is tasdiq, and that what is meant by it is that which reaches the level of submission (idh'ān) and acceptance, and the meaning called 'bāwurden' (Persian for belief) applies to it, so that it is decisive tasdiq, we do not concede that it does not admit variation. Rather, certainty has ranks from the most evident of self-evident truths to the most hidden of theoretical ones, and [the text breaks off]...
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage continues the debate on whether faith increases and decreases, focusing on Imam al-Haramayn's (Juwayni's) argument and a subsequent objection and response. The passage is a mix of argument, objection, and response. It begins by quoting Juwayni: If faith is tasdiq, no tasdiq can be superior to another, just as no knowledge is superior to knowledge. But if faith is defined as obedience, then increase and decrease are plausible. Then an objection is considered: if faith is works, it is even more unlikely to admit increase and decrease, because there is no rank above the whole and no one could complete it. The response clarifies that this objection only refutes the Mu'tazili view that faith is negated by omission of works, not the Salafi view that faith remains as long as tasdiq remains; the variation then pertains to perfection, not essence. Then al-Razi's reconciliation is cited: verses indicating non-variation refer to the essence, and those indicating variation refer to the perfect form. Then a stronger objection is raised: tasdiq itself can vary in strength and weakness, as with different degrees of certainty about different propositions, and this variation applies to faith because it is a tasdiq of what the prophet brought, whether general or detailed. The response counters that obligatory tasdiq must reach the level of certainty, which supposedly does not vary. But the final argument denies that certainty does not vary, because certainty has ranks from the most evident to the most hidden. The passage ends mid-sentence, likely continuing this point.

Correction: Juwayni allows variation in the perfection of faith, not its essence.

Are you personally troubled by the apparent contradiction between the constancy of tasdiq and the ups and downs of your spiritual life? How will you let this reconciliation reshape your understanding of your own journey with Allah?

Objection that tasdiq varies and the response about certainty.

Certainty itself has degrees, so tasdiq can vary.

Two Definitions of Iman: Tasdiq and Obedience
Imam al-Haramayn discusses two definitions of iman and their implications for increase and decrease.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two definitions of iman discussed by Imam al-Haramayn and their implications for whether iman increases or decreases.

Core Idea
How you define iman determines whether it can increase or decrease.

Imam al-Haramayn presents two competing definitions of iman: as inner assent (tasdiq) or as outward and inward obedience. Each definition leads to a different conclusion about the possibility of increase and decrease in faith. This passage lays out both positions, along with which one the author prefers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once. Notice the two conditional statements: 'If we interpret iman as tasdiq...' and 'Whoever interprets it as obedience...'.
The passage is concise; each phrase carries weight.
2
Compare the two definitions
Consider the implications: tasdiq is uniform and cannot vary, while obedience can vary in degree. This is the root of the debate on increase and decrease of iman.
Think about why assent might be seen as binary.
3
Note the author's stance
The passage ends with 'we do not prefer this', indicating a preference for the tasdiq definition. Reflect on why the author might prefer a definition that precludes increase/decrease.
The author's preference shapes later theological discussions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال إمام الحرمين : إذا حملنا الإيمان على التصديق ، فلا يفضل تصديق تصديقاً، كما لا يفضل علم علماً . ومن حمله على الطاعة سراً وعلناً ـ وقد مال إليه القلانسي (١) ـ فلا يبعد إطلاق القول بأنه يزيد بالطاعة، وينقص بالمعصية، ونحن لا نؤثر هذا
And Imam al-Haramayn said: If we interpret iman as tasdiq (assent), then one tasdiq does not excel another tasdiq, just as knowledge does not excel knowledge. And whoever interprets it as obedience secretly and openly—and al-Qalanisi inclined to this—then it is not far to state that it increases with obedience and decreases with disobedience, but we do not prefer this.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage presents two definitions of iman (faith) and their consequences for whether iman can increase or decrease. Imam al-Haramayn states that if iman is defined as tasdiq (inner assent), then one instance of tasdiq cannot be superior to another, just as one instance of knowledge cannot be superior to another knowledge (meaning assent is uniform). If iman is defined as obedience (both secret and open acts)—a view to which al-Qalanisi inclined—then it is plausible to say that iman increases with obedience and decreases with disobedience. However, the author (al-Taftazani or the commentator) says, "We do not prefer this." The passage thus sets up the debate by contrasting two foundational interpretations.

Iman as Works: Objection and Answer on Increase
Objection and answer on increase of iman as works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the objection against iman increasing is refuted by distinguishing between the essence and perfection of iman.

Core Idea
Iman's essence stays; only its perfection grows.

This passage tackles a tricky objection: if iman equals works, how can it increase? The answer shows that only the Mu'tazili view falls, while the Salaf view holds iman's core constant, with increase in its perfection. We'll unpack both sides.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice how the objection is stated firmly.
The objection uses 'لا يقال' introducing a hypothetical critique.
2
Note the two arguments
The objection gives two reasons: 1) no rank above 'all' to be increase, and 2) no one completes all works, so increase in the incomplete is impossible. Identify these in the text.
3
Identify the two theological positions
The answer distinguishes between the Mu'tazila view (iman lost by sin) and the Salaf view (iman remains as long as tasdiq remains). Which view does the objection actually refute?
The answer says the objection only refutes the Mu'tazili view.
4
Grasp the essence vs perfection distinction
The answer concludes that increase and decrease apply to kamal (perfection) of iman, not asl (essence). Understand why this resolves the objection for the Salaf view.
This is the key takeaway.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يقال: الإيمان على تقدير كونه اسماً للأعمال أولى بأن لا يحتمل الزيادة والنقصان . أما أولاً فلأنه لا مرتبة فوق الكل ليكون زيادة، ولا إيمان دونه ليكون نقصاناً. وأما ثانياً، فلأن أحداً لا يستكمل الإيمان حينئذ، والزيادة على ما لم يكمل بعد محال . لأنا نقول هذا إنما يرد على من يقول بانتفاء الإيمان بانتفاء شيء من الأعمال أو التروك، كما هو مذهب المعتزلة، لا على من يقول ببقائه ما بقي التصديق، كما هو مذهب السلف، إلا ان الزيادة والنقصان على هذا تكون في كمال الإيمان لا في أصله .
It cannot be said: Iman, on the assumption that it is a name for works, is more deserving of not admitting increase and decrease. First, because there is no rank above 'all' to be an increase, and no iman below it to be a decrease. Second, because no one would then complete iman, and increase in what has not been completed is impossible. For we say: This objection only applies to one who says that iman ceases with the omission of any work or abandonment, as is the doctrine of the Mu'tazila, not to one who says that it remains as long as tasdiq remains, as is the doctrine of the Salaf. However, increase and decrease on this view are in the perfection of iman, not in its essence.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer. The objection argues that if iman is defined as works, then it should be even more impossible for it to increase or decrease. Two reasons are given: first, there is no rank above 'all works' to constitute an increase, and no iman below it to constitute a decrease; second, no one ever completes all works, so increase in what is incomplete is impossible. The answer distinguishes between two positions. The objection only refutes those who say iman disappears if any work is missing—the Mu'tazila view. It does not refute those who say iman remains as long as tasdiq (assent) remains—the Salaf view. In the Salaf view, increase and decrease pertain to the perfection (kamal) of iman, not its essence (asl). Thus, iman's essence remains constant, but its completeness waxes and wanes.

كَمَال
مُعْتَزِلَة
سَلَف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the objection proves iman cannot increase at all.
Correction: The answer shows it only refutes the Mu'tazili view, not the Salaf view.

Checkpoint

A) The Mu'tazili view that iman ceases with sin.
B) The Salaf view that iman remains as long as tasdiq remains.
C) The view that iman is only works.
D) The view that iman is only tasdiq.

Key Takeaway
Iman's essence (tasdiq) does not increase or decrease; only its perfection varies with works.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Salaf saw increase and decrease as a matter of perfection. Are you actively seeking to perfect your iman, or are you content with just having its essence? What concrete step will you take today to grow in perfection?

Al-Razi's Reconciliation on Iman's Variation
Imam al-Razi reconciles two positions on iman's variation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Razi reconciles the two positions on iman by distinguishing its essence from its perfection.

Core Idea
Iman's essence is unchanging; its perfection varies.

The debate on whether iman varies or not has apparent contradictions in texts. Imam al-Razi offers a subtle resolution by differentiating between the core reality of iman and its higher manifestations. This passage presents his concise reconciliation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the English translation. Notice the key terms 'asl' (essence) and 'kamil' (perfect).
The passage is dense despite its brevity.
2
Identify the two categories
Al-Razi distinguishes between 'asl' (essence) and 'kamil' (perfect). Identify which evidence corresponds to each by reading the text carefully.
The word 'masruf' (directed) is crucial to see the mapping.
3
Understand the reconciliation logic
Reflect on why this resolves the apparent contradiction: both sets of texts are true, but they speak about different aspects of iman. The unchanging essence and the variable perfection coexist.
4
Connect to the broader debate
Consider how this resolution fits into the larger discussion on whether iman increases and decreases. Al-Razi's distinction allows both positions to hold without conflict.
This is a classic example of tawfiq (harmonization) in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولهذا قال الإمام الرازي وجه التوفيق أن ما يدل على أن الإيمان لا يتفاوت مصروف الى أصله وما يدل على أنه يتفاوت مصروف إلى الكامل منه
And for this reason Imam al-Razi said: The face of reconciliation is that what indicates that iman does not vary is directed to its essence, and what indicates that it does vary is directed to the perfect of it.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This is a short but significant passage where Imam al-Razi (Fakhr al-Din al-Razi) provides a reconciliation (tawfiq) between apparently contradictory evidence. He states that texts which indicate that iman does not vary are to be understood as referring to its essence (asl), while texts which indicate that it does vary refer to the perfect form (al-kamil) of iman. Thus, both sets of evidence are true but apply to different aspects of iman: its unchanging core and its variable completeness.

Key Terms
تَوْفِيق
أَصْل
كَامِل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think al-Razi is creating a contradiction by saying iman both varies and does not vary.
Correction: He is harmonizing texts by showing they refer to different aspects: the unchanging essence and the variable perfection.

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Razi, what does the statement that iman does not vary refer to?
A) The perfect form of iman.
B) The essence of iman.
C) The works of iman.
D) The increase of iman.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Razi shows that iman's essence is invariant while its perfection admits degrees.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you examine your own faith, do you sense that its core is secure even when your actions waver? How does al-Razi's distinction between essence and perfection help you understand the times you feel your faith is weak without despairing that you've lost it entirely? What one specific action will you take this week to move your faith from its bare essence toward its perfect form?
?
If iman's essence is unchanging, do you risk becoming complacent and neglecting growth? Where in your life have you settled for the 'essence' of faith without striving for perfection? Write down one area where you will intentionally seek to increase the perfection of your iman, starting tomorrow.
?
Al-Razi's reconciliation shows that both sets of evidence are true. How does this teaching challenge any tendency you have to view your faith as either all-or-nothing or as hopelessly inconsistent? What is one concrete change in your daily routine that would reflect a deeper commitment to growing the perfection of your iman?

Does Tasdiq Vary? Objection and Response
Objection that tasdiq varies and the response on degrees of certainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that tasdiq varies in strength and the response that certainty itself has degrees, supported by scriptural evidence.

Core Idea
Certainty is not uniform; it ranges from clearest truths to hidden theories.

Having established that tasdiq is a single act, a critic objects: does it not vary in strength? After all, believing the sun rises differs from believing the world was created. This passage presents the objection and the reply, which distinguishes tasdiq from certainty and shows that even certainty admits degrees.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the first part of the passage where the objector claims that tasdiq varies in strength and gives examples.
Notice the examples: sun rising (strong) vs. world's creation (weaker).
2
Identify the counter-objection mentioned
The passage then considers a possible response: that required tasdiq is certainty which does not vary. Find this counter-objection.
It begins with 'لا يقال'.
3
Analyze the author's reply
The author refutes the counter-objection by distinguishing certainty from tasdiq and then arguing that certainty has degrees.
Note the two pieces of evidence: Abraham's request and Ali's statement.
4
Consider the final point about dominant opinion
The passage ends by questioning whether only certainty counts, hinting that dominant opinion (ghalib al-zann) might also be valid.
This is a more advanced point; understand that it opens further discussion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولقائل أن يقول : لا نسلم أن التصديق لا يتفاوت، بل يتفاوت قوة وضعفاً، كما في التصديق بطلوع الشمس، والتصديق بحدوث العالم، لأنه إما نفس الاعتقاد القابل للتفاوت أو مبني عليه وقلة وكثرة ، كما في التصديق الإجمالي والتفصيلي الملاحظ لبعض التفاصيل وأكثر وأكثر ، فإن ذلك من الإيمان لكونه تصديقاً بما جاء به النبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) إجمالاً فيما علم إجمالاً ، وتفصيلاً فيما علم تفصيلاً، لا يقال : الواجب تصديق يبلغ حد اليقين، وهو لا يتفاوت لأن التفاوت لا يتصور إلا باحتمال النقيض، لأنا نقول : اليقين من باب العلم والمعرفة، وقد سبق أنه غير التصديق، ولو سلم أنه التصديق، وأن المراد به ما يبلغ حد الإذعان والقبول، ويصدق عليه المعنى المسمى «بكرويدن» ليكون تصديقاً قطعياً، فلا نسلم أنه لا يقبل التفاوت بل لليقين مراتب من أجلى البديهيات إلى أخفى النظريات، وكون التفاوت راجعاً إلى مجرد الجلاء والخفاء غير مسلم، بل عند الحصول وزوال التردد التفاوت بحالة ، وكفاك قول الخليل الله مع ما كان له من التصديق : ولكن ليطمئن قلبي ) وعن علي (رضي الله عنه) : لو كشف الغطاء ما ازددت يقيناً . على أن القول بأن المعتبر في حق الكل هو اليقين وأن ليس للظن الغالب الذي لا يخطر معه النقيض بالبال حكم اليقين محل نظر
And one may say: We do not concede that tasdiq does not vary; rather, it varies in strength and weakness, as in the tasdiq of the sun's rising and the tasdiq of the world's coming into existence, because it is either itself belief that admits variation or based on it, and in paucity and abundance, as in general and detailed tasdiq, observing some details and more and more. For that is part of iman, being tasdiq of what the Prophet (peace be upon him) brought, generally in what is known generally, and in detail in what is known in detail. It cannot be said: The required tasdiq reaches the level of certainty, and it does not vary because variation can only be conceived with the possibility of the opposite. For we say: Certainty (yaqin) is of the category of knowledge and cognition, and it has preceded that it is other than tasdiq. And if it is conceded that it is tasdiq, and that what is meant by it is what reaches the level of submission and acceptance, and the meaning called 'bakroydan' is true of it, so that it is conclusive tasdiq, still we do not concede that it does not accept variation; rather, certainty has levels from the clearest self-evident truths to the most hidden theoretical matters. And that variation is merely a matter of clarity and obscurity is not conceded; rather, upon attainment and removal of hesitation, variation persists. And sufficient for you is the saying of al-Khalil (Abraham), despite his tasdiq: 'But so that my heart may be at ease' (Quran 2:260); and from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him): 'If the veil were lifted, I would not increase in certainty.' Moreover, the statement that what is considered for everyone is certainty and that dominant opinion (ghalib al-zann) with which no opposite occurs to the mind does not have the ruling of certainty is a point of reflection.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This long passage is a detailed objection and answer. The objector argues that tasdiq itself does vary in strength and weakness, using examples like believing the sun will rise (strong) versus believing the world was created (weaker). Tasdiq can be general or detailed, and thus the amount of detail causes variation. The objector then addresses a counter-objection: one might say that the required tasdiq must be certain (yaqin), and certainty does not vary. The answer is that certainty (yaqin) is different from tasdiq; even if it were the same, certainty has degrees from clearest self-evident truths to hidden theoretical ones. The attempt to reduce variation to merely clarity vs. obscurity is rejected; variation is real. Evidence is given: Prophet Abraham (peace be upon him) asked for reassurance despite his tasdiq, and Ali said he would not increase in certainty even if the veil were lifted. Thus, even highest certainty can vary. Finally, the idea that only certainty counts and that dominant opinion (ghalib al-zann) does not have the same ruling is questioned.

يَقِين
قُوَّة
ضَعْف
إِجْمَال
تَفْصِيل
ظَنّ غَالِب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Certainty is uniform and does not admit any variation.
Correction: The passage shows that certainty has levels from the clearest truths to the most hidden, and even prophets and imams expressed variation in certainty.

Checkpoint
What evidence does the author give to show that certainty (yaqin) has degrees?
A) The example of the sun rising.
B) Abraham's request for reassurance and Ali's statement.
C) The distinction between general and detailed tasdiq.
D) The definition of iman as works.

Key Takeaway
Tasdiq and certainty both admit variation, and even the highest certainty has degrees, as shown by prophetic and saintly examples.

?
The lesson ends by questioning whether dominant opinion has the same ruling as certainty. In your daily life, do you act on dominant opinions that should be certainties—like the truth of the Quran or the Hereafter? What is one area where you need to elevate your certainty from mere assumption to unshakable conviction?

The Rational Proof for Iman's Increase and Decrease
Sanusi presents a rational proof by absurdity for the variability of iman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument (reductio ad absurdum) used to prove that iman increases and decreases.

Core Idea
If iman never varied, every believer's faith would equal that of prophets—an absurd conclusion.

The proponents of the view that iman increases and decreases did not rely solely on scripture; they also employed rational reasoning. In this lesson, we examine their logical argument, which is a classic reductio ad absurdum. The argument is simple but powerful: if iman were uniform, then the faith of the worst sinner would match that of the greatest prophet. Since this is impossible, iman must vary.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic and translation of the rational argument. Notice the structure: they mention reason and transmission, then present the rational argument.
The passage begins with 'احتج القائلون بالزيادة والنقصان بالعقل والنقل. أما العقل فلأنه...'
2
Understand the reductio
The argument assumes the opposite (no variation) and deduces an impossible consequence (equal iman of a sinful person and a prophet). Therefore, the assumption is false.
This is a proof by contradiction.
3
Apply the logic
Think about the purpose: to establish that iman can differ among believers. How does this argument help?
4
Note the key term 'tasdiq'
The argument equates iman with tasdiq (affirmation). The equality would be in tasdiq. That is important for understanding the debate.
Tasdiq is a core component in defining iman.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
احتج القائلون بالزيادة والنقصان بالعقل والنقل. أما العقل فلأنه لو لم يتفاوت، لكان إيمان آحاد الأمة، بل المنهمك في الفسق مساو بالتصديق الأنبياء والملائكة واللازم باطل قطعاً. وأما النقل فلكثرة النصوص الواردة في هذا المعنى قال الله تعالى : وإذا تليت عليهم آياته زادتهم إيمانا ) (۱) ليزدادوا إيماناً مع إيمانهم ) (۲) ويزداد الذين آمنوا إيماناً (۳) ( وما زادهم إلا إيماناً وتسليماً (٤) ( فأما الذين آمنوا فزادتهم إيماناً " (٥) وعن ابن عمر رضي الله تعالى عنه : قلنا : يا رسول الله ، إن الإيمان هل يزيد وينقص ؟ قال : نعم ، يزيد حتى يدخل صاحبه الجنة، وينقص حتى يدخل صاحبه النار» (٦). وعن عمر (رضي الله تعالى عنه ، وروي مرفوعاً: «لووزن إيمان أبي بكر بإيمان
The proponents of increase and decrease argued by reason and transmission. As for reason, because if it did not vary, then the iman of the common people, even the one engrossed in sin, would be equal in tasdiq to the prophets and angels, and the implication is absolutely false. As for transmission, because of the many texts that have come concerning this meaning. Allah the Exalted said: 'And when His verses are recited to them, they increase them in faith' (8:2); 'that they may increase in faith upon their faith' (48:4); 'and He will increase those who believe in faith' (74:31); 'and it only increased them in faith and submission' (33:22); 'but as for those who believe, it increased them in faith' (9:124). And from Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with him): 'We said: O Messenger of Allah, does iman increase and decrease? He said: Yes, it increases until its owner enters Paradise, and it decreases until its owner enters the Fire.' And from Umar (may Allah be pleased with him), and it is narrated as marfu': 'If the iman of Abu Bakr were weighed against the iman...'
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage presents two categories of argument for the view that iman increases and decreases: rational and scriptural. The rational argument is a reductio: if iman did not vary, then the iman of ordinary people, even persistent sinners, would be equal in tasdiq to that of prophets and angels—an obviously false conclusion. Therefore, iman must vary. The scriptural argument cites multiple Quranic verses that explicitly mention increase in iman: Surah al-Anfal 8:2, al-Fath 48:4, al-Muddaththir 74:31, al-Ahzab 33:22, and al-Tawba 9:124. Additionally, a hadith from Ibn Umar reports the Prophet confirming that iman increases and decreases, with the extreme outcomes of Paradise and Fire. A hadith from Umar (likely incomplete in the text) begins a comparison of Abu Bakr's iman with others, implying superiority.

Key Terms
عَقْل
زِيَادَة
نُقْصَان
تَصْدِيق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The rational argument is merely speculative and not a valid proof.
Correction: The argument is a formal reductio ad absurdum: it shows that denying variation leads to an obvious absurdity, thus proving the claim.

Checkpoint
What consequence follows if iman did not vary, according to the rational argument?
A) Everyone would have the same iman.
B) The iman of sinners would equal that of prophets.
C) Iman would be meaningless.
D) Prophets would have less iman.

Key Takeaway
The rational proof for iman's increase and decrease is a reductio: if iman were fixed, the faith of the most sinful would equal that of the prophets, which is absurd; therefore iman must vary.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider your own life: Have you used the idea that 'iman is in the heart' as an excuse to neglect actions, believing your faith remains the same regardless? How does Sanusi's proof challenge that assumption? What commitment can you make today to actively seek increase in your iman?
?
If the iman of the most sinful equals that of the prophets, as the absurd conclusion suggests, then why should you strive to obey Allah? How does the variability of iman motivate you to repent and improve? What specific step will you take this week to increase your tasdiq?
?
Reflect on a time when you felt your faith was weak. Did you assume that was just a temporary feeling that didn't affect the reality of your iman? How does understanding that iman actually varies change your responsibility? Will you now seek means of increase? What is the first thing you will change?

The Scriptural Proof for Iman's Increase and Decrease
The author adduces multiple scriptural proofs (Quran and hadith) for the increase and decrease of iman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Quranic verses and hadith that support the view that iman increases and decreases.

Multiple Quranic verses and prophetic traditions explicitly state that iman increases.

Additionally, they bring a hadith in which the Prophet directly affirms that iman increases and decreases, even indicating the extreme outcomes. This lesson surveys these textual proofs.

3
Understand the hadith
The hadith from Ibn Umar is a direct question and answer. What does the Prophet say about the extremes?
Increase leads to Paradise, decrease leads to Fire.
4
Reflect on cumulative weight
The author says 'many texts' — consider how this scriptural evidence complements the rational argument.

Transmitted Proofs for Increase and Decrease of Faith
Author cites Quranic verses and hadiths as transmitted proofs for variation in faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key Quranic verses and hadiths that serve as transmitted evidence for the increase and decrease of faith.

Core Idea
The Quran and hadith explicitly affirm that faith increases and decreases.

After discussing rational proofs for variation in faith, the author now turns to transmitted evidence from revelation. The abundance of Quranic verses and prophetic hadiths provides clear textual support for the doctrine that faith is not static but can grow or diminish. This lesson presents those primary texts along with early scholarly commentary.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage fully
Read the Arabic and translation carefully, noting the list of Quranic verses and hadiths. The OCR may make the verse references unclear, but the overall meaning is preserved.
The verse numbers are garbled in the source; focus on the hadiths which are clearer.
2
Identify the three categories of evidence
The passage includes Quranic verses (though garbled), a hadith from Bukhari, comments by Ibn Battal, and the hadith of Ibn Umar and Umar. Recognize the different types.
3
Reflect on the implication
Understand that the transmitted evidence supports the Ash'ari view of faith's variability, and note the nuance that the root assent cannot decrease but can increase.
Ibn Battal's comment clarifies that the core assent remains intact.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما النقل فلكثرة النصوص الواردة في هذا المعنى قال الله تعالى : (سورة البقرة آية رقم ٢٦٠ . (۲) سورة الأنفال آية رقم ۲ . (٣) سورة الفتح آية رقم ٤ . (4) سورة المدثر آية رقم ۳۱ . (۵) سورة الأحزاب آية رقم ٢٢ . (٦) سورة التوبة آية رقم ١٢٤ . (۷) الحديث : أخرجه الإمام البخاري في كتاب الايمان ۳۳ باب زيادة الإيمان ونقصانه وقول الله تعالى: وزدناهم هدى . ويزداد الذين آمنوا إيمانا ) وقال : واليوم أكملت لكم دينكم ، فإذا ترك شيئاً من الكمال فهو ناقص . قال ابن بطال التفاوت في التصديق على قدر العلم والجهل فمن قل علمه كان نصديقه مثلاً بمقدار ذرة والذي فوقه في العلم تصديق بمقدار برة أو شعيرة إلا أن أصل التصديق الحاصل في قلب كل أحد منهم لا يجور عليه النقصان، ويجوز عليه الزيادة. وعن ابن عمر رضي الله تعالى عنه : قلنا : يا رسول الله ، إن الإيمان هل يزيد وينقص ؟ قال : نعم ، يزيد حتى يدخل صاحبه الجنة، وينقص حتى يدخل صاحبه النار» (۷). وعن عمر (رضي الله تعالى عنه ، وروي مرفوعاً: «لو وزن إيمان أبي بكر بإيمان هذه الأمة، لرجح به»(۱)
As for transmission: because of the abundance of texts reported in this meaning. Allah the Exalted said: (Surah al-Baqarah verse number 260. (2) Surah al-Anfal verse number 2. (3) Surah al-Fath verse number 4. (4) Surah al-Muddaththir verse number 31. (5) Surah al-Ahzab verse number 22. (6) Surah at-Tawbah verse number 124. (7) The hadith: Narrated by Imam al-Bukhari in the Book of Faith, chapter 33 on increase and decrease of faith and the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'And we increased them in guidance. And those who believe increase in faith.' And he said: 'Today I have perfected your religion for you.' So if one leaves something of perfection, it is deficiency. Ibn Battal said: Variation in assent is according to knowledge and ignorance; he whose knowledge is little, his assent is like the amount of a speck, and he who is above him in knowledge, his assent is like a grain or a barley seed, except that the root of assent in the heart of every one of them does not admit of decrease, but increase is possible. And from Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with him): we said: O Messenger of Allah, does faith increase and decrease? He said: Yes, it increases until its owner enters Paradise, and decreases until its owner enters Hellfire. And from Umar (may Allah be pleased with him), raised as a marfu' narration: 'If the faith of Abu Bakr were weighed against the faith of this Ummah, it would outweigh it.'
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage presents the transmitted (نقلي) evidence for the increase and decrease of faith. The author first notes the abundance of texts. The verse citations (though garbled in the OCR) are from the Quran, such as 'those who believe increase in faith' (Surah al-Muddaththir 31) and others. The hadiths include a statement from Ibn Umar asking the Prophet (peace be upon him) whether faith increases and decreases; the Prophet affirms it, saying it can increase until Paradise and decrease until Hell. Another hadith from Umar states that Abu Bakr's faith outweighs the entire Ummah. The passage also includes an explanation by Ibn Battal that variation in assent corresponds to knowledge, and the root assent can increase but not decrease—though the overall consensus supports variation.

نصوص

نقصان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That transmitted proofs claim faith can decrease to complete loss or that it remains static.
Correction: The hadith of Ibn Umar shows faith can decrease, but the root assent remains; it does not disappear entirely (it decreases 'until Hellfire', implying preservation of some faith). Also, the increase and decrease are affirmed, countering the static view.

Checkpoint
What did the Prophet say about faith when asked if it increases and decreases?
A) It only increases
B) It only decreases
C) It increases until Paradise and decreases until Hell
D) It remains constant

Key Takeaway
The Quran and hadith provide explicit transmitted evidence that faith can increase and decrease, with the root assent remaining intact.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
Ibn Battal linked the depth of assent to knowledge. Are you actively studying your deen to increase your certainty? If not, what is stopping you, and what small step can you take this week?

Three Ways Faith Can Increase
The author gives three interpretations of increasing faith that preserve its essential unity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three interpretations of how faith can increase without implying that the core act of assent (tasdiq) itself varies.

Core Idea
Faith increases in duration, objects, or effects—but its essence remains one.

This passage presents three explanations (wujuh) for how faith can be said to increase, defending the view that the core act of assent (tasdiq) is not inherently variable. These explanations reinterpret verses and arguments about increase in faith, showing that increase can refer to continuity, the number of objects believed, or the fruits of faith. Let's examine each one.

Guided Path
1
First interpretation: increase by continuity
Read the first answer: faith increases by the duration and constancy of assent. Notice how this makes the Prophet's faith superior due to its uninterrupted continuity.
This answers the objection that obtaining a new instance after none is not a real increase.
2
Second interpretation: increase by objects of faith
Read the second answer: faith increases as more specific obligations are revealed and believed. This means faith can grow in detail.
This does not require time-specific revelation; it applies to all times.
3
Third interpretation: increase by effects
Read the third answer: faith increases by its fruit and light in the heart, which strengthen with obedience and weaken with sin.
This is the most straightforward interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأجيب بوجوه : الأول - أن المراد الزيادة بحسب الدوام والثبات وكثرة الأزمان والساعات. وهذا ما قال إمام الحرمين : النبي ( ) يفضل من عداه باستمرار تصديقه وعصمة الله إياه من مخامرة الشكوك، والتصديق عرض لا يبقى، فيقع المنبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) متوالياً ولغيره على الفترات، فثبت للنبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) أعداد من الإيمان لا يثبت لغيره إلا بعضها، فيكون إيمانه أكثر ، والزيادة بهذا المعنى مما لا نزاع فيه . وما يقال : إن حصول المثل إليه بعد انعدام الشيء لا يكون زيادة فيه، مدفوع بأن المراد زيادة اعداد حصلت وعدم البقاء لا ينافي ذلك. الثاني - أن المراد الزيادة بحسب زيادة المؤمن به، والصحابة كانوا آمنوا في الجملة، وكان يأتي فرض بعد فرض وكانوا يؤمنون بكل فرض خاص. وحاصله أن الإيمان واجب إجمالاً فيما علم إجمالاً ، وتفصيلاً فيما علم تفصيلاً. والناس متفاوتون في ملاحظة التفاصيل كثرة وقلة ، فيتفاوت إيمانهم زيادة ونقصاناً، ولا يختص ذلك بعصر النبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) على ما يتوهم . الثالث - أن المراد زيادة ثمرته وإشراق نوره في القلب . فإنه يزيد بالطاعات، وينقص بالمعاصي . وهذا مما لا خفاء فيه . وهذه الوجوه جيدة في التأويل لو ثبت لهم أن التصديق في نفسه لا يقبل التفاوت والكلام فيه .
And it was answered with aspects: The first—that what is meant is increase in terms of continuity, constancy, and abundance of times and hours. This is what Imam al-Haramayn said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) is superior to others by the continuity of his assent and Allah's protection of him from the occurrence of doubts, and assent is an accident that does not endure, so it occurs for the Prophet (peace be upon him) consecutively and for others intermittently. Thus the Prophet (peace be upon him) has a number of instances of faith that others do not possess except some, so his faith is greater, and increase in this meaning is uncontested. And what is said—that obtaining a similar thing after the thing's nonexistence is not an increase in it—is refuted: the intended meaning is an increase in the number of instances that occurred, and lack of endurance does not contradict that. The second—that what is meant is increase in terms of the object of faith being increased: the Companions believed in general, and one obligation after another would come, and they would believe in each specific obligation. The gist is that faith is obligatory in general regarding what is known generally, and in detail regarding what is known in detail. People vary in their observation of details in number and scarcity, so their faith varies increase and decrease, and this is not specific to the time of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as may be imagined. The third—that what is meant is the increase of its fruit and the radiance of its light in the heart. For it increases by acts of obedience and decreases by sins. This is something without concealment. And these aspects are good for interpretation if they established that assent itself does not admit of variation—though discussion remains.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage presents three interpretations (وجوه) of the increase and decrease of faith, offered as answers to those who argue that faith increases. The first interpretation (الأول) is that increase refers to continuity and duration: the Prophet's faith is continuous, while others' is intermittent; thus the total instances of faith are more for the Prophet. This refutes the objection that gaining a new instance after the old one ceases is not a real increase. The second interpretation (الثاني) is that increase refers to the objects of faith: as new obligations are revealed, believers affirm each specifically, so faith increases in number of details affirmed. The third interpretation (الثالث) is that increase refers to the effects and light of faith in the heart, which strengthens with obedience and weakens with sin. The author notes that these interpretations are valid if one holds that the core assent (تصديق) itself does not inherently vary—but that point remains debated.

أعداد
مؤمن به
ثمرة
نور
طاعات
معاصي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some argue that faith cannot increase at all because the core act of assent is uniform and unchanging.
Correction: This passage shows that faith can increase in meaningful ways—by continuity, by objects of faith, or by its effects—without implying that the act of assent itself varies in intensity or quality.

Checkpoint
According to the second interpretation, when does faith increase?
A) By continuous duration of assent
B) By affirming each new obligation specifically
C) By the light of faith in the heart
D) By performing more prayers

Key Takeaway
Faith can increase in duration, specificity of objects, or effects, without altering the essence of tasdiq.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of the three interpretations—continuity, object detail, or fruit/light—do you see most lacking in your own faith? What is one specific action you can take today to increase your faith in that area?
?
The Prophet's faith is described as continuous while ours is intermittent. When was the last time you consciously renewed your assent to God's commands? How can you make your faith more continuous, even if only in small steps?
?
Your faith's fruit and light increase with obedience and decrease with sins. Is there a sin you are holding onto that is dimming that light? What would it cost you to abandon it and regain the radiance?

The Exception in Professing Faith
Sanusi introduces the debate on exception in faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the debate over whether it is permissible to say 'if Allah wills' when professing faith, and the reasoning behind both positions.

Core Idea
Saying 'if Allah wills' about one's faith is not doubt, but humility.

The question of whether a believer can say 'I am a believer, if Allah wills' has been debated among scholars. Some see it as a sign of proper reliance on Allah, while others view it as a dangerous expression of doubt. This passage introduces the two sides and sets the stage for the arguments to come.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the parentheses in the Arabic; they may indicate a heading.
2
Identify the two positions
The passage presents two views: the preferred doctrine (al-madhhab) that exception is valid and may even be preferable, and the majority view that it is forbidden.
3
Understand the majority's objection
The majority forbid it because it indicates doubt (shakk) or at least gives the impression of doubt (īhām). Ask yourself: why would saying 'if Allah wills' imply doubt?
Consider the context of faith being a matter of certainty.
4
Recognize the author's promise of arguments
The author ends by saying 'and we have [our] arguments' – indicating that counterarguments will follow. Think about what arguments might support the permissibility.
This prepares us for the next part of the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : المبحث الرابع (المذهب صحة الاستثناء في الإيمان، حتى إنه ربما يؤثر أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله على أنا مؤمن حقاً، ومنعه الأكثرون لدلالته على الشك أو إيهامه إياه. لا أقل، ولنا وجوه .
He said: The Fourth Section. The doctrine [is] the validity of exception in [professing] faith, such that sometimes saying 'I am a believer, if Allah wills' is preferred over saying 'I am a believer truly.' But most [scholars] forbid it because it indicates doubt or gives the impression of doubt—at the very least. And we have [our own] arguments.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage inaugurates a new section (المبحث الرابع) on the permissibility of using الاستثناء (exception) in statements of faith, i.e., saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills' (أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله) rather than an unqualified 'I am a believer truly' (أنا مؤمن حقاً). The author states that the preferred view (المذهب) is that such exception is valid and may even be preferable. However, the majority (الأكثرون) forbid it because it implies doubt or at least gives the impression of doubt. The author then indicates that there are counterarguments: 'we have [our] aspects (وجوه).' The passage ends abruptly, so the detailed arguments are expected on subsequent pages.

Key Terms
استثناء
إيمان
شك
إيهام
مذهب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Saying 'if Allah wills' about one's faith shows doubt in Allah's power or in one's own faith.
Correction: The exception is not about doubting Allah's power but about acknowledging that one's faith is not self-generated—it is a gift from Allah that could be taken away.

Checkpoint
Why do most scholars forbid saying 'I am a believer, if Allah wills'?
A) Because it is a lie
B) Because it indicates doubt or creates that impression
C) Because it is not in the Quran
D) Because it implies faith can decrease

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of using exception in professing faith is contested, with the majority fearing doubt, while the author suggests it may be preferable and promises arguments.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'I am a believer', do you ever feel a tension between certainty and humility? How does the exception 'if Allah wills' challenge you to be honest about the source of your faith?
?
The majority feared that exception implies doubt. Do you have hidden doubts about your faith that you are afraid to acknowledge? What would it mean for you to say 'I am a believer if Allah wills' as an act of trust rather than uncertainty?
?
If you truly believed that your faith is entirely a gift from Allah, how would that change the way you speak about your faith to others? Would the phrase 'if Allah wills' become a natural expression of humility, or do you rely on confident declarations to reassure yourself?

Three Answers on the Increase of Faith
Author gives three interpretations for increase in faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three scholarly interpretations of how faith can increase: in duration and constancy, in the objects of belief, and in its fruits and light in the heart.

Core Idea
Faith increases in duration, detail, and intensity — not quantity.

Scholars affirm that faith can increase, but they differ on what that increase means. Is it a quantitative increase in the substance of faith? Or is it about constancy, depth, and obedience? This passage presents three classic answers that protect the doctrine that faith is not a created thing that grows like a physical object.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English carefully. Notice the author lists three 'wujuh' (aspects).
The passage begins with 'Wa ujiba bi wujuh'.
2
Understand the first answer
The first answer interprets increase in terms of duration and constancy, citing Imam al-Haramayn. Understand why continuity matters and how the objection about non-continuity is rebutted.
This answer focuses on the Prophet's continuous faith.
3
Understand the second answer
The second answer interprets increase as increase in the objects of belief. As new obligations come, believers affirm them, increasing the number of specific beliefs held.
This applies to all believers, not just the Prophet's time.
4
Understand the third answer
The third answer interprets increase as increase in the fruits and light of faith in the heart, varying with obedience and sin.
This is a common understanding.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The author notes that these interpretations are good if one holds that assent itself does not admit of variation. Consider why this condition is needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأجيب بوجوه : الأول - أن المراد الزيادة بحسب الدوام والثبات وكثرة الأزمان والساعات. وهذا ما قال إمام الحرمين : النبي ( ) يفضل من عداه باستمرار تصديقه وعصمة الله إياه من مخامرة الشكوك، والتصديق عرض لا يبقى، فيقع النبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) متوالياً ولغيره على الفترات، فثبت للنبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) أعداد من الإيمان لا يثبت لغيره إلا بعضها، فيكون إيمانه أكثر ، والزيادة بهذا المعنى مما لا نزاع فيه . وما يقال : إن حصول المثل إليه بعد انعدام الشيء لا يكون زيادة فيه، مدفوع بأن المراد زيادة اعداد حصلت وعدم البقاء لا ينافي ذلك. الثاني - أن المراد الزيادة بحسب زيادة المؤمن به، والصحابة كانوا آمنوا في الجملة، وكان يأتي فرض بعد فرض وكانوا يؤمنون بكل فرض خاص. وحاصله أن الإيمان واجب إجمالاً فيما علم إجمالاً ، وتفصيلاً فيما علم تفصيلاً. والناس متفاوتون في ملاحظة التفاصيل كثرة وقلة ، فيتفاوت إيمانهم زيادة ونقصاناً، ولا يختص ذلك بعصر النبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) على ما يتوهم . الثالث - أن المراد زيادة ثمرته وإشراق نوره في القلب . فإنه يزيد بالطاعات، وينقص بالمعاصي . وهذا مما لا خفاء فيه . وهذه الوجوه جيدة في التأويل لو ثبت لهم أن التصديق في نفسه لا يقبل التفاوت والكلام فيه .
And it was answered with aspects: The first – that the intended [increase] is increase in terms of duration, constancy, and multiplicity of times and hours. This is what Imam al-Haramayn said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) is superior to others through the continuity of his assent and Allah's protection of him from the intrusion of doubts, and assent is an accident that does not subsist, so for the Prophet (peace be upon him) it occurs continuously and for others at intervals; thus for the Prophet (peace be upon him) numbers of faith are established that for others only some of them are established, so his faith is more, and increase in this sense is indisputable. And what is said: that the occurrence of the like to him after the non-existence of a thing is not an increase in it is rebutted by [saying] that what is meant is an increase in numbers that occurred, and non-continuity does not negate that. The second – that what is meant is increase according to the increase in the object of belief, and the Companions believed in general, and there came obligation after obligation, and they believed in each specific obligation. And its summary is that faith is obligatory in general regarding what is known in general, and in detail regarding what is known in detail. And people differ in observing the details in abundance and scarcity, so their faith varies in increase and decrease, and that is not specific to the era of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as might be imagined. The third – that what is meant is the increase of its fruit and the shining of its light in the heart. For it increases with acts of obedience and decreases with sins. And this is not hidden. And these aspects are good in interpretation if it is established for them that assent itself does not admit of variation, and the discussion is about that.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage presents three answers interpreting the meaning of 'increase in faith' in response to an objection. The first answer interprets increase in terms of duration and constancy: the Prophet's faith is continuous while others experience gaps, so his faith is numerically more. The second interprets increase as increase in the objects of belief: as new obligations come, believers affirm them, leading to more detailed faith. The third interprets increase as increase in the fruits and light of faith in the heart, which varies with obedience and sin. The passage concludes that these interpretations are good if one holds that assent itself does not admit of variation, which is the point of contention.

التصديق
إمام الحرمين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Increase in faith means the substance of faith grows larger.
Correction: Scholars interpret increase in terms of duration, objects of belief, and fruits, not as quantitative growth of a substance.

Checkpoint
According to the third answer, how does faith increase or decrease?
A) By the quantity of objects believed
B) By its duration and continuity
C) By its fruits and light in the heart, through obedience and sin
D) It does not increase or decrease

Key Takeaway
Faith increases in duration, in the number of specific beliefs, and in its practical effects, but not in its essential reality.

The Validity of Exception in Faith and Its Proofs
Author states the ruling on istithna in faith and gives three proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ruling on making exceptions in declaring one's faith (istithna) and the three proofs provided for its validity.

Core Idea
Istithna in faith is valid; it expresses humility, not doubt.

In this passage, the author presents the position that it is permissible, even preferable, to say 'I am a believer if Allah wills' rather than asserting absolute certainty. The majority opposed this, seeing it as indicative of doubt. The author counters by offering three proofs that explain the true intent behind such phrasing.

Guided Path
1
Read the ruling and the majority's objection.
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the author's statement that the madhhab is the validity of exception, and that the majority forbade it due to apparent doubt.
2
Understand the first proof: seeking blessing and politeness.
The first proof explains that saying 'if Allah wills' is a form of seeking blessing (tabarruk) and politeness (ta'adub), not an expression of doubt.
3
Understand the second proof: saving faith is hidden.
The second proof states that true saving faith (iman al-munji) is a hidden matter; one can never be fully certain that no contrary element has contaminated it, so one refers it to God's will.
4
Grasp the third proof: doubt concerns the final state of faith.
The third and most relied-upon proof clarifies that the doubt is about the faith at the time of death (iman al-muwafaat), not about one's current faith (iman al-najiz).
This is the key distinction.
5
Appreciate the distinction between current faith and saving faith.
The author then emphasizes that calling final faith the criterion does not deny the reality of current faith; it only denies its salvific power. The same applies to disbelief, happiness, and misery.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : المبحث الرابع (المذهب صحة الاستثناء في الإيمان، حتى إنه ربما يؤثر أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله على أنا مؤمن حقاً، ومنعه الأكثرون لدلالته على الشك أو إيهامه إياه. لا أقل، ولنا وجوه . الأول - أنه للتبرك والتأدب، لا للشك والتردد . والثاني - أن الإيمان المنجي أمر خفي، لا يأمن الجازم بحصوله أن يشوبه شيء من المنافيات من حيث لا يعلم، فيفوضه إلى المشيئة. الثالث - وعليه التعويل، أنه للشك فيما هو آية النجاة، وهو إيمان الموافاة، لا في الإيمان الناجز . وليس معنى قولهم : العبرة بإيمان الموافاة أن الناجز ليس بإيمان حقيقة . بل إنه ليس بمنج . وكذا الكفر والسعادة والشقاوة . فالسعيد سعادة الموافاة لا يتغير إلى شقاوة الموافاة، وإنما التغير في (الناجز .
He said: The fourth section. (The madhhab is the validity of exception in faith, such that perhaps saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills' is preferred over 'I am a believer truly', and the majority forbade it because it indicates doubt or gives the impression of it. That is the least, and we have proofs. The first – that it is for blessing and politeness, not for doubt and hesitation. The second – that saving faith is a hidden matter; one who is certain of its occurrence is not secure that something contrary might contaminate it without his knowledge, so he refers it to the will. The third – and on it reliance, that it is for doubt concerning that which is the sign of salvation, which is the faith of the final state (iman al-muwafaat), not concerning current faith (iman al-najiz). And it is not the meaning of their statement: 'Consideration is given to the faith of the final state' that current faith is not real faith. Rather, it is not saving. And similarly for disbelief, happiness, and misery. So the happy person with the happiness of the final state does not change to the misery of the final state, and change only occurs in the current state.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage introduces the fourth topic, the ruling on making exceptions in declaring one's faith (istithna). It states that the madhhab is that such exception is valid, even to the extent that saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills' may be preferred over 'I am a believer truly'. The majority forbade it because it suggests doubt. The author then provides three proofs: first, it is for seeking blessing and politeness, not doubt; second, saving faith is hidden and one cannot be certain it is free from defects, so one refers it to God's will; third (relied upon), the doubt is about the faith at the time of death (iman al-muwafaat), not about current faith. It clarifies that considering the final state does not negate the reality of current faith but only its salvific power.

Key Terms
الاستثناء في الإيمان
إيمان الموافاة
إيمان الناجز
المنجي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Istithna indicates doubt in one's current faith.
Correction: The doubt is about the final state of faith (iman al-muwafaat), not about current faith.

Checkpoint
According to the third proof, what is the doubt in istithna about?
A) The existence of God
B) Whether one is currently a believer
C) The faith at the time of death (iman al-muwafaat)
D) The truth of Islam

Key Takeaway
Istithna in faith is valid because it either seeks blessing, acknowledges the hidden nature of saving faith, or expresses uncertainty about one's final state, not current belief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever said 'I am a believer if Allah wills' with genuine humility, or do you resist because you fear it sounds weak? What does this reveal about your trust in your own deeds versus Allah's grace?
?
If your salvation depends on your faith at the moment of death, are you living today with that urgency? Or do you assume your current piety guarantees your end?
?
The passage teaches that even your current faith, though real, may be contaminated without your knowledge. Does this thought make you examine your heart daily? If not, why not?

Salaf Views on Istithna and the Objection to the First Proof
Author reports Salaf view on istithna and rebuts first proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Salaf's differing positions on whether faith admits exception (istithna) and the key objection to the first proof for its permissibility.

Core Idea
The debate over istithna is not about permissibility but about preference and exclusivity of etiquette.

This passage presents the classical disagreement over whether one may say 'I am a believer if Allah wills.' While some Salaf permitted it as a form of politeness, the majority forbade it to avoid any suggestion of doubt. The objection to the first proof challenges its justification for preferring the exception over a direct statement.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two positions on istithna
Identify the Salaf who allowed saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills' and the majority (including Abu Hanifa) who forbade it.
The key figures are al-Shafi'i and Ibn Mas'ud for permission, and Abu Hanifa and his companions for prohibition.
2
Grasp the majority's rationale
The majority argue that faith is definite assent; hesitation would negate faith. Therefore, they consider it better to avoid the exception and say 'I am a believer truly.'
This is based on the nature of assent being certain.
3
Examine the first proof for istithna
Those who permit istithna give reasons: to seek blessing, show politeness to Allah's will, and avoid self-praise. The objection points out that this only establishes validity, not preference.
The objection is the main focus of the second part.
4
Analyze the objection in detail
The objection states that the first proof fails to show that the exception is preferable over the direct statement, nor does it remove suspicion of doubt, nor does it justify why this etiquette is specific to faith.
This is the core of the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذهب كثير من السلف، وهو المحكي عن الشافعي (رضي الله تعالى عنه) والمروي عن ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه أن الإيمان يدخله الاستثناء، فيقال : أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله تعالى. ومنعه الأكثرون وعليه أبو حنيفة (رضي الله عنه) وأصحابه، لأن التصديق أمر معلوم لا تردد فيه عند تحققه، ومن تردد في تحققه له ، لم يكن مؤمناً، قطعاً، وإذا لم يكن للشك والتردد، فالأولى أن يترك ، بل يقال : أنا مؤمن حقاً . دفعاً للإيهام . وللقائلين بصحته وجوه : الأول - أنه للتبرك في ذكر الله والتأدب بإحالة الأمور إلى مشيئة الله ، والتبرؤ عن تزكية النفس والإعجاب بحالها والتردد في العاقبة والمآل وهذا يفيد مجرد الصحة، لا إيثار قولهم : أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله على أنا مؤمن حقاً، ولا يدفع ما ذكر من دفع الإيهام، ولا يبين وجه اختصاص التأدب والتبرك بالإيمان دون غيره من الأعمال والطاعات
Many of the Salaf went, and it is reported from al-Shafi'i (may Allah be pleased with him) and related from Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) that faith admits exception, so one may say: 'I am a believer if Allah wills.' And the majority forbade it, and Abu Hanifa (may Allah be pleased with him) and his companions held that, because assent is a known matter, there is no hesitation in it when it is realized, and whoever hesitates in its realization is definitely not a believer. And if it is not for doubt and hesitation, then it is better to leave it, rather one should say: 'I am a believer truly,' to remove the impression of doubt. And for those who claim its validity there are proofs: the first – that it is for blessing in mentioning Allah and politeness by referring matters to Allah's will, and for disowning self-praise and admiration of one's state and hesitation about the consequence and outcome. But this yields mere validity, not preference for saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills' over 'I am a believer truly', nor does it remove the aforementioned removal of the impression of doubt, nor does it clarify why politeness and blessing are specific to faith and not to other acts of obedience.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage reports the view of many Salaf, including al-Shafi'i and Ibn Mas'ud, that exception in faith is permissible, allowing one to say 'I am a believer if Allah wills'. The majority, including Abu Hanifa, forbid it because assent is known without doubt and hesitation would negate faith. They argue it should be avoided. The passage then presents an objection to the first proof given by those who permit istithna: the proof that it is for blessing and politeness only establishes permissibility, not preference over the straightforward statement, does not remove the impression of doubt, and does not explain why this etiquette is exclusive to faith.
